## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: materials science / constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, which is a core problem in solid mechanics and materials science. Stress typically increases with strain (elasticity + hardening) and decreases with increasing temperature (thermal softening).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime, small strains)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (elastic modulus decreasing with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon-type strain hardening)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (combined hardening and thermal effects)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Ludwik with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (temperature-dependent Ludwik model)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (saturation hardening with thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (combined hardening and thermal softening)
- Arrhenius thermal factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (thermally activated deformation)
- Linear thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - T) (modulus linear in temperature)
- Polynomial hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (polynomial stress-strain curve)
- Swift model with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (Swift hardening with thermal factor)
- Hyperbolic sine (Garofalo): sigma = c0 * T * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (creep/high-temperature deformation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening saturation → Use (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or epsilon/(epsilon + c) to capture diminishing hardening rate
- Thermal softening as multiplicative factor → Separate sigma into f(epsilon) * g(T) where g(T) is a decreasing function of T
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation → exp(c/T) appears when deformation is controlled by thermally activated dislocation processes
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 representing initial yield stress before hardening: sigma = c0 + f(epsilon)
- Homologous temperature scaling → Temperature enters as (1 - c*T**c1) representing fraction of melting temperature
- Concave-up to concave-down transition in stress-strain → Swift model (epsilon + c0)**c1 captures initial rapid then gradual hardening
- Strain-temperature coupling → At higher temperatures, hardening exponent may decrease: epsilon**(c0 + c1*T) or similar coupled forms
- Elastic-plastic transition → Piecewise or smooth transition using tanh(c*epsilon) to blend linear elastic and saturated plastic regimes
